      1. Path Traversal (1)
        1. POST https://host.docker.internal/wp-login.php
          Alert tags
          • OWASP_2021_A01
          • POLICY_SEQUENCE =
          • CWE-22
          • PCI_DSS
          • WSTG-v42-ATHZ-01
          • POLICY_DEV_FULL =
          • POLICY_QA_STD =
          • POLICY_QA_FULL =
          • POLICY_PENTEST =
          • HIPAA
          • OWASP_2017_A05
          • POLICY_DEV_STD =
          Alert description

          The Path Traversal attack technique allows an attacker access to files, directories, and commands that potentially reside outside the web document root directory. An attacker may manipulate a URL in such a way that the web site will execute or reveal the contents of arbitrary files anywhere on the web server. Any device that exposes an HTTP-based interface is potentially vulnerable to Path Traversal.

          Most web sites restrict user access to a specific portion of the file-system, typically called the "web document root" or "CGI root" directory. These directories contain the files intended for user access and the executable necessary to drive web application functionality. To access files or execute commands anywhere on the file-system, Path Traversal attacks will utilize the ability of special-characters sequences.

          The most basic Path Traversal attack uses the "../" special-character sequence to alter the resource location requested in the URL. Although most popular web servers will prevent this technique from escaping the web document root, alternate encodings of the "../" sequence may help bypass the security filters. These method variations include valid and invalid Unicode-encoding ("..%u2216" or "..%c0%af") of the forward slash character, backslash characters ("..\") on Windows-based servers, URL encoded characters "%2e%2e%2f"), and double URL encoding ("..%255c") of the backslash character.

          Even if the web server properly restricts Path Traversal attempts in the URL path, a web application itself may still be vulnerable due to improper handling of user-supplied input. This is a common problem of web applications that use template mechanisms or load static text from files. In variations of the attack, the original URL parameter value is substituted with the file name of one of the web application's dynamic scripts. Consequently, the results can reveal source code because the file is interpreted as text instead of an executable script. These techniques often employ additional special characters such as the dot (".") to reveal the listing of the current working directory, or "%00" NULL characters in order to bypass rudimentary file extension checks.

          Parameter 
          redirect_to
          Attack 
          wp-login.php
          Solution

          Assume all input is malicious. Use an "accept known good" input validation strategy, i.e., use an allow list of acceptable inputs that strictly conform to specifications. Reject any input that does not strictly conform to specifications, or transform it into something that does. Do not rely exclusively on looking for malicious or malformed inputs (i.e., do not rely on a deny list). However, deny lists can be useful for detecting potential attacks or determining which inputs are so malformed that they should be rejected outright.

          When performing input validation, consider all potentially relevant properties, including length, type of input, the full range of acceptable values, missing or extra inputs, syntax, consistency across related fields, and conformance to business rules. As an example of business rule logic, "boat" may be syntactically valid because it only contains alphanumeric characters, but it is not valid if you are expecting colors such as "red" or "blue."

          For filenames, use stringent allow lists that limit the character set to be used. If feasible, only allow a single "." character in the filename to avoid weaknesses, and exclude directory separators such as "/". Use an allow list of allowable file extensions.

          Warning: if you attempt to cleanse your data, then do so that the end result is not in the form that can be dangerous. A sanitizing mechanism can remove characters such as '.' and ';' which may be required for some exploits. An attacker can try to fool the sanitizing mechanism into "cleaning" data into a dangerous form. Suppose the attacker injects a '.' inside a filename (e.g. "sensi.tiveFile") and the sanitizing mechanism removes the character resulting in the valid filename, "sensitiveFile". If the input data are now assumed to be safe, then the file may be compromised.

          Inputs should be decoded and canonicalized to the application's current internal representation before being validated. Make sure that your application does not decode the same input twice. Such errors could be used to bypass allow list schemes by introducing dangerous inputs after they have been checked.

          Use a built-in path canonicalization function (such as realpath() in C) that produces the canonical version of the pathname, which effectively removes ".." sequences and symbolic links.

          Run your code using the lowest privileges that are required to accomplish the necessary tasks. If possible, create isolated accounts with limited privileges that are only used for a single task. That way, a successful attack will not immediately give the attacker access to the rest of the software or its environment. For example, database applications rarely need to run as the database administrator, especially in day-to-day operations.

          When the set of acceptable objects, such as filenames or URLs, is limited or known, create a mapping from a set of fixed input values (such as numeric IDs) to the actual filenames or URLs, and reject all other inputs.

          Run your code in a "jail" or similar sandbox environment that enforces strict boundaries between the process and the operating system. This may effectively restrict which files can be accessed in a particular directory or which commands can be executed by your software.

          OS-level examples include the Unix chroot jail, AppArmor, and SELinux. In general, managed code may provide some protection. For example, java.io.FilePermission in the Java SecurityManager allows you to specify restrictions on file operations.

          This may not be a feasible solution, and it only limits the impact to the operating system; the rest of your application may still be subject to compromise.

										<div class="contextual-help-sidebar">
						<p><strong>For more information:</strong></p><p><a href="https://wordpress.org/documentation/article/dashboard-screen/">Documentation on Dashboard</a></p><p><a href="https://wordpress.org/support/forums/">Support forums</a></p><p><a href="https://wordpress.org/documentation/wordpress-version/version-6-9-4/">Version 6.9.4</a></p>					</div>
					
					<div class="contextual-help-tabs-wrap">
						
							<div id="tab-panel-overview" class="help-tab-content active">
								<p>Welcome to your WordPress Dashboard!</p><p>The Dashboard is the first place you will come to every time you log into your site. It is where you will find all your WordPress tools. If you need help, just click the &#8220;Help&#8221; tab above the screen title.</p>							</div>
							
							<div id="tab-panel-help-navigation" class="help-tab-content">
								<p>The left-hand navigation menu provides links to all of the WordPress administration screens, with submenu items displayed on hover. You can minimize this menu to a narrow icon strip by clicking on the Collapse Menu arrow at the bottom.</p><p>Links in the Toolbar at the top of the screen connect your dashboard and the front end of your site, and provide access to your profile and helpful WordPress information.</p>							</div>
							
							<div id="tab-panel-help-layout" class="help-tab-content">
								<p>You can use the following controls to arrange your Dashboard screen to suit your workflow. This is true on most other administration screens as well.</p><p><strong>Screen Options</strong> &mdash; Use the Screen Options tab to choose which Dashboard boxes to show.</p><p><strong>Drag and Drop</strong> &mdash; To rearrange the boxes, drag and drop by clicking on the title bar of the selected box and releasing when you see a gray dotted-line rectangle appear in the location you want to place the box.</p><p><strong>Box Controls</strong> &mdash; Click the title bar of the box to expand or collapse it. Some boxes added by plugins may have configurable content, and will show a &#8220;Configure&#8221; link in the title bar if you hover over it.</p>							</div>
							
							<div id="tab-panel-help-content" class="help-tab-content">
								<p>The boxes on your Dashboard screen are:</p><p><strong>Welcome</strong> &mdash; Shows links for some of the most common tasks when setting up a new site.</p><p><strong>Site Health Status</strong> &mdash; Informs you of any potential issues that should be addressed to improve the performance or security of your website.</p><p><strong>At a Glance</strong> &mdash; Displays a summary of the content on your site and identifies which theme and version of WordPress you are using.</p><p><strong>Activity</strong> &mdash; Shows the upcoming scheduled posts, recently published posts, and the most recent comments on your posts and allows you to moderate them.</p><p><strong>Quick Draft</strong> &mdash; Allows you to create a new post and save it as a draft. Also displays links to the 3 most recent draft posts you've started.</p><p><strong>WordPress Events and News</strong> &mdash; Upcoming events near you as well as the latest news from the official WordPress project and the <a href="https://planet.wordpress.org/">WordPress Planet</a>.</p>							</div>
												</div>
				</div>
			</div>
		<div id="screen-options-wrap" class="hidden" tabindex="-1" aria-label="Screen Options Tab">

			Some screen elements can be shown or hidden by using the checkboxes.			Expand or collapse the elements by clicking on their headings, and arrange them by dragging their headings or by clicking on the up and down arrows.		</p>

		</div>

			var initialize  = function() {
				var init, id, inPostbox, $wrap;
				var readyState = document.readyState;

				if ( readyState !== 'complete' && readyState !== 'interactive' ) {
					return;
				}

				for ( id in tinyMCEPreInit.mceInit ) {
					if ( initialized.indexOf( id ) > -1 ) {
						continue;
					}

					init      = tinyMCEPreInit.mceInit[id];
					$wrap     = tinymce.$( '#wp-' + id + '-wrap' );
					inPostbox = $wrap.parents( '.postbox' ).length > 0;

						! init.wp_skip_init &&
						( $wrap.hasClass( 'tmce-active' ) || ! tinyMCEPreInit.qtInit.hasOwnProperty( id ) ) &&
						( readyState === 'complete' || ( ! inPostbox && readyState === 'interactive' ) )
					) {
						tinymce.init( init );
						initialized.push( id );

						if ( ! window.wpActiveEditor ) {

					tinymce.$( '.wp-editor-wrap ' ).removeClass( 'tmce-active' ).addClass( 'html-active' );

						initialize();
					} else {

          Solution

          Remove the private IP address from the HTTP response body. For comments, use JSP/ASP/PHP comment instead of HTML/JavaScript comment which can be seen by client browsers.

          The page includes mixed content, that is content accessed via HTTP instead of HTTPS.

<main class="wp-block-group has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="margin-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
	<h1 class="wp-block-query-title">Archives: <span>Imported Items</span></h1>
	 
	
<div class="wp-block-query alignfull is-layout-flow wp-block-query-is-layout-flow">
	<ul class="alignfull wp-block-post-template is-layout-flow wp-block-post-template-is-layout-flow"><li class="wp-block-post post-66 imported_item type-imported_item status-publish hentry">
		
		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/project-management-professional-pmp-certification-exam-prep-course-mce-opd-c-pmpprep/" target="_self" >Project Management Professional (PMP)® Certification Exam Prep Course &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-PMPPREP</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Project Management Professional (PMP)&reg; Certification Exam Prep Course<br />
MCE-OPD-C-PMPPREP</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>Our PMP&reg; Exam Prep Course is tailored for professionals with project management experience who are ready to earn the industry-leading PMP&reg; certification. Whether you&rsquo;re seeking a boost in your career or looking to validate your skills, this course will provide you with the knowledge, tools, and strategies to pass the PMP&reg; certification exam with confidence. We make complex project management concepts simple and accessible through expert instruction and practical exam strategies proven to work.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Course Materials and Benefits:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><strong>PMI&rsquo;s Exclusive Course Materials</strong>: Get access to PMI-authorized content that will deepen your understanding of the exam material.</li>
<li><strong>Blue Summit LMS</strong>: Our custom LMS platform features exclusive Blue Summit content, including exam strategies and practice questions.</li>
<li><strong>Mock Exams</strong>: Take full-length, timed mock exams to simulate the real PMP&reg; certification exam experience and test your readiness.</li>
<li><strong>Instructor Support</strong>: Enjoy year-long, asynchronous instructor support to help you address any questions and stay on track.</li>
<li><strong>Application Assistance</strong>: Get expert help with navigating and completing your PMP&reg; certification exam application.</li>
<li><strong>Weekly Exam Review Sessions</strong>: Participate in live, instructor led review sessions to go over key topics and answer exam related sessions.</li>
<li><strong>One-Year PMI&reg; Membership: </strong>Get full access to PMI&reg; resources, networking opportunities, and career tools.</li>
<li><strong>One Free Certification Exam: </strong>Receive one free attempt at the PMP&reg; certification exam as part of your course enrollment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Exclusive Benefits:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Year-Long Support</strong>: Post-training, get access to our instructors for up to one year for additional guidance and assistance.</li>
<li><strong>Proven Exam Strategies</strong>: We provide tips and techniques designed to help you manage time and succeed on exam day.</li>
<li><strong>Ongoing Course Updates</strong>: We keep our materials aligned with the latest PMP&reg; exam changes so you&rsquo;re always prepared.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Who Should Enroll:</strong></p>
<p>This course is ideal for experienced project managers looking to validate their skills and knowledge through PMP&reg; certification. It is perfect for professionals in industries such as IT, construction, healthcare, defense, and more.</p>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Note: By registering for this course, you will be subscribed to our newsletter and other communications to receive updates and resources about future courses. You can unsubscribe at any time.</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>
<p>Leadership and Professional Development</p>
</div>
			<div style="margin-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--40);" class="wp-block-post-date has-small-font-size"><time datetime="2026-04-03T00:52:29+00:00"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/project-management-professional-pmp-certification-exam-prep-course-mce-opd-c-pmpprep/">April 3, 2026</a></time></div>

		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/business-process-analysis-mce-opd-c-busipaid/" target="_self" >Business Process Analysis    &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-BUSIPAID</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Business Process Analysis<br />
MCE-OPD-C-BUSIPAID</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>An organization&rsquo;s greatest assets are its people and its products or services. However, good products and good people are not enough to keep an organization competitive.&nbsp;Its core processes determine the real competitive advantage of an organization. Bloated, inefficient, ineffective processes, laden with non-value-added work and waste, affect an organization&rsquo;s ability to deliver &ldquo;value&rdquo; to their customers in a timely and cost-effective way. This course will teach you&nbsp;how to identify and eliminate non-value-added work, innovate, and streamline processes.</p>
<p><strong>Why You Should Attend</strong><br />
Inefficient, ineffective, and outdated processes impact an organization&rsquo;s ability to maintain customer loyalty and satisfaction, as well as employee productivity, satisfaction, and retention. This course will teach&nbsp;you how to streamline your existing processes to deliver value to your customers, both internal and external.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Who Should Attend</strong><br />
This course is ideal for anyone responsible for ensuring an organization&rsquo;s success in meeting customers&rsquo; and key stakeholder needs, as well as teams that are currently responsible for streamlining existing processes.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A digital version of student materials and supplemental handouts&nbsp;</li>
<li>21 PDUs/2.1 CEUs</li>
<li>A certificate of attendance from NC State University</li>
</ul>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Note: By registering for this course, you will be subscribed to our newsletter and other communications to receive updates and resources about future courses. You can unsubscribe at any time.</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>

		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/finance-and-engineering-economics-for-engineers-mce-opd-c-zmfaee/" target="_self" >Finance and Engineering Economics for Engineers &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-ZMFAEE</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Finance and Engineering Economics for Engineers<br />
MCE-OPD-C-ZMFAEE</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>Engineers cannot see their designs come to fruition, take shape, and be implemented without the acquisition of necessary funds. Since most engineering curricula don&rsquo;t include significant financial analysis and engineering economics skill dissemination, this course fills that gap. In this course, you learn about finance, engineering economics, and corporate reporting requirements. Engineers need to be able to, objectively and quantitatively, show the advantages and disadvantages of various engineering design options to their clients and employers. After all that is the <strong>2nd Code of Engineering Ethics </strong>requirement for all<strong> Licensed Professional Engineers</strong>. One way to view the value of this course is to see it as a &ldquo;Crash MBA&rdquo; Course for Engineers, Professionals, and Managers. This course is themed after a book published by the instructor, Prof. Rauf, titled: &#8220;Finance and Accounting for Energy Engineers,&#8221; published through River Publishers. In this course, you learn to perform time value of money calculations using equations or financial factor tables explained in a simple and easy to understand way, illustrated through practical examples, just the way Prof. Rauf does in his book. You will learn asset depreciation methods and their influence on net profit and taxes. Learn about the widely used and accepted capital investment performance metrics, such as financial ratios, payback period, breakeven, and NPV, etc. You learn about fundamental accounting methods: The Income Statement and the Balance Sheet. You will get an appreciation of the role played by inventory systems in the control of net income, net profits and tax liability. Life cycle cost and other cost classifications in industrial and commercial organizations are covered. This course is designed for engineers, professional engineers, energy professionals, engineering managers, technical professionals, facilities &nbsp;managers and other professionals who are not intimately familiar or current on finance, accounting, time value of money analysis, and engineering economics principles and practices. Participants are kept engaged through questions and answers, discussions and classwork. Board acceptance guarantee.</p>
<p><strong>Who Should Attend?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Professional Engineers</li>
<li>Manufacturing Managers</li>
<li>Facility Managers&nbsp;</li>
<li>Project and Program Managers</li>
<li>Maintenance Managers</li>
<li>Energy Engineers and other Energy Professionals</li>
<li>Engineering Managers</li>
<li>Construction Managers</li>
<li>Architects</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>8 PDHs/0.8&nbsp;CEUs&nbsp;(7.5 PDHs for NYS Lic.)</li>
<li>Reference notebook with activities</li>
<li>Certificate&nbsp;of completion from NC&nbsp;State University</li>
</ul>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p>Course Outline</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Finance, Engineering Economics and Accounting Concepts:</strong> Definitions, Discussion and Examples of Calculations.<br />
	a) Economics and engineering economics&nbsp;<br />
	b) Common Organizational Structures &#8211; Role of Financial Analysts, Accountants, Controllers and CFO&rsquo;s</li>
<li><strong>Income Statements and Balance Sheets. </strong>Cash Flow and Working Capital Concepts 3</li>
<li><strong>Financial Reporting Requirements </strong></li>
<li><strong>Financial Metrics and Ratios: </strong>Payback Period, FV, PV, Time Value of Money Conversions and Analyses. IRR, ROI, NPV, ROE, ROR, Current Ratio, Acid Test Ratio, Plant Turnover Ratio<strong> </strong></li>
<li><strong>Depreciation Alternatives: </strong>S/L, Prod. Based, SOY Digits.<strong> </strong></li>
<li><strong>Inventory Concepts: </strong>FIFO, LIFO, EOQ, Inv. Turnover Ratio, WIP Inv., Inv. Carrying Costs.<strong> </strong></li>
<li><strong>Lease vs. Buy Decisions. </strong>Repair vs. Replace Decisions</li>
<li><strong>Costs: </strong>Life Cycle Cost. Period Costs, Direct and Indirect Costs.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
</ul>

			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/ediscovery-mce-opd-n-zgedp/" target="_self" >eDiscovery &#8211; MCE-OPD-N-ZGEDP</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>eDiscovery<br />
MCE-OPD-N-ZGEDP</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>The Advanced Paralegal: eDiscovery topic is an introductory course for persons entering the eDiscovery field, as well as professionals wanting to broaden their knowledge of the eDiscovery process. This 7 week course covers the entire eDiscovery process, from preparation, to collection, to review of Electronically Stored Information (ESI). Throughout the 17 online modules and tests, learners will progress through the basics of eDiscovery preparation, best practices for ESI collection, and finally, the review process. The course is supplemented with a comprehensive textbook that covers most relevant eDiscovery topics.</p>
<p><strong>Required textbooks for this course:</strong></p>
<p><em>eDiscovery for Paralegals Manual</em></p>
<p>The required text is an e-book included in your course fee. You will access the book from your course home page.</p>

			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/foundations-of-agile-project-management-mce-opd-c-fagilepm/" target="_self" >Foundations of Agile Project Management &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-FAGILEPM</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Foundations of Agile Project Management<br />
MCE-OPD-C-FAGILEPM</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>To be agile is to be able to think and move quickly and easily.&nbsp;To project managers, Agile describes how they deal with uncertainty and an ever-changing environment. Agile is a doctrine or way of thinking that was conceived as an alternative to the waterfall methodology by a group of software programmers who moved from the traditional, sequential waterfall approach to methods dependent/reliant on customer feedback and iterative, incremental adjustment throughout the development lifecycle. Popular in the tech world and beyond, Agile is a movement within project management that seeks to improve collaboration and response rates while anticipating complexity and change. Agile can denote any number of methodologies: Kanban, Scrum, XP, DevOps, SAFe<sup>&reg;</sup>, Crystal, and LSD. This course does not promote or focus on a single methodology.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Why You Should Attend</strong>&nbsp;<br />
You should attend this course to expand your PM toolkit by learning Agile methods for managing projects with a high degree of uncertainty, are rapidly changing, and require a lot of customer involvement.&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition, an interdisciplinary instructor with many years of real-world experience involving different project management methodologies who can supplement the course materials with relevant examples and coaching teaches this course.</p>
<p><strong>Who Should Attend</strong>&nbsp;<br />
This course is intended for individuals and/or organizations that have a fundamental level of project management knowledge and that are managing IT-related projects or projects with a high degree of unknown in rapidly changing environments.&nbsp;It is a great &ldquo;first&rdquo; or foundational class for those planning to explore other Agile methodologies.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<ul>
<li>A course workbook with reference materials (pdf format for download)</li>
<li>21 PDUs/2.1 CEUs</li>
<li>A certificate of attendance from NC&nbsp;State University</li>
</ul>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Note: By registering for this course, you will be subscribed to our newsletter and other communications to receive updates and resources about future courses. You can unsubscribe at any time.</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>
<p>Leadership and Professional Development</p>

	</li><li class="wp-block-post post-77 imported_item type-imported_item status-publish hentry">
		
		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/electrical-engineering-principles-and-practices-for-non-electrical-engineers-mce-opd-c-eenee/" target="_self" >Electrical Engineering Principles and Practices for Non-Electrical Engineers &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-EENEE</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Electrical Engineering Principles and Practices for Non-Electrical Engineers<br />
MCE-OPD-C-EENEE</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p><em>If there is no course available, please sign up for the</em> <a href="https://reporter.ncsu.edu/link/courseview?courseID=MCE-OPD-C-EENEE&amp;deptName=MCE">&#128065;Watchlist</a> <em>to be notified when a course opens.</em></p>
<p>This seminar or course covers principles of electricity in a simple, easy to understand format. It is themed after a book published by the instructor, titled: &ldquo;Electrical Engineering for non-Electrical Engineers.&rdquo; In the book, as well as this seminar, Rauf uses simple analogies and practical, day to day, examples to illustrate the, otherwise, abstract concepts of electrical engineering. For instance, the analogies of fluid pressure and elevation difference are used to explain the role and significance of electrical voltage, aka&nbsp;electromotive potential. &nbsp;Upon attending this course, participants will be able to perform straightforward and common calculations associated with voltage, current, resistance, impedance, circuit analysis, DC, single phase AC, three phase AC, power, power factor, service factor, load factor, reactance, and much more. Practical examples of electrical equipment applications, in industrial, commercial and institutional settings, are covered. Discussions on electrical equipment, components, safety electronic devices, and test instrumentation are included. Important concepts in electrical safety are introduced. Participants are introduced to electrical drawing types and standards. A brief introduction to NEC, National Electrical Code and NFPA 70 E, the arc flash code is provided. This course is designed for engineers, licensed professional engineers, energy professionals, engineering managers, technical professionals, facilities managers and other professionals who are not intimately familiar or current on electrical engineering principles and practices. No prerequisite required. Since this course takes you from fundamentals on up, even non-engineers &ndash; with some math and science background &#8211; can take away a commensurate amount of electrical engineering knowledge. Board acceptance guarantee. Participants are kept engaged through questions and answers, discussions and classwork.</p>
<p><strong>Who Should Attend</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Licensed Professional Engineers</strong> (PEs)&nbsp;who need to meet the annual or biennial license renewal PDH (Professional Development Hour) or CEU (Continuing Education Unit) requirements</li>
<li><strong>Engineers and Architects</strong> who do not possess current working knowledge of electrical engineering</li>
<li><strong>Facility Managers, Engineering Managers, Program/Project Managers and other executives</strong> or leaders who feel a lack of adequate electrical knowledge to hold meaningful discussions and to make informed decisions with interacting with their electrical subordinates or colleagues</li>
<li><strong>Non-engineers</strong>, including <strong>technical writers</strong>,<strong> </strong>responsible for developing operations and maintenance manuals for electrical or electrically operated equipment</li>
<li><strong>Procurement/purchasing professionals</strong> who are responsible for acquisition of electrical or electrically operated equipment</li>
<li>Candidates aspiring to take the <strong>FE or PE exams</strong></li>
<li><strong>Energy Managers and Construction Managers</strong></li>
<li><strong>Maintenance Engineers</strong> and <strong>Maintenance Managers</strong></li>
<li><strong>Patent attorneys</strong> and attorneys who specialize in construction, workplace safety workmanship litigation cases</li>
<li><strong>Other professionals</strong> whose annual <strong>PLP, Performance and Learning Program</strong>,<strong> </strong>includes engineering/technical courses/seminars/workshops</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive&nbsp;</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>8.0 PDHs/0.8&nbsp;CEUs&nbsp;(7.5 PDHs for NYS Lic.)</li>
<li>Reference notebook with activities</li>
<li>Networking break and luncheon for in-person participants</li>
<li>Certificate of completion from NC&nbsp;State University</li>
</ul>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Why you shouldn&rsquo;t miss this course &ndash; how this course can benefit you,&nbsp;your organization, and what is unique about this course:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Have you ever felt somewhat inadequate and ill-equipped in your<strong> technical discussions with electrical engineers and electricians</strong>? If so, then this course or seminar is a must.<br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li>Do you, as an engineer, manager, or technician, <strong>feel that your knowledge and understanding of the difference between AC and DC electricity</strong> is inadequate or insufficient, then you must not miss this seminar?<br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li>How often do you get a chance to attend a workshop, course, or a seminar that is presented by the author of the book on the subject matter &#8211; live? In this seminar, you will have the opportunity to interact and learn from <strong>Bobby Rauf, the author of the text, titled, &ldquo;Electrical Engineering for Non-Electrical Engineers.&rdquo;</strong> (A copy of the book available at additional cost)<br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li>As an engineer, technician or manager <strong>have you ever found the concept of power factor, horsepower, apparent power, reactive power, real power, three phase versus single phase elusive</strong> and hard to comprehend? Then, this seminar will present an excellent opportunity to remedy that.<br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li><strong>Imagine yourself, as an engineer or manager, at 2 o&#8217;clock in the morning, in a triage situation, leading a team, trying to get electrical equipment up and running.</strong> You and your team members have electrical drawings of different types spread out, but, without the <strong>electrical engineering</strong> background, the symbol and nomenclature appear foreign to you. This seminar is an opportunity for you to bridge that gap.<br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li>How often do you get an <strong>opportunity to understand abstract and complex electrical concepts through relatively simple analogies and explanation</strong>? This seminar will provide you that invaluable opportunity.<br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li>Some workshops and seminars end up being monotonous monologues from the presenter to the audience. Not this one. <strong>In this seminar, you will get an opportunity to exercise the skills and concepts through classwork and engage the instructor in discussions.</strong><br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li>Do you manage or work with electrical engineers or electricians, and <strong>are rusty in electrical engineering concepts, analytical techniques and design considerations, or are completely unfamiliar with them? This seminar provides you the opportunity to brush up on those knowledge and skills, so that you can understand the challenges confronted by your subordinates and colleagues more clearly and can make informed decisions.</strong><br />
	&nbsp;</li>
<li><strong>Last, but not least &ndash;</strong> If you are <u><strong>not</strong></u> a licensed Professional Engineer, but aspire to be one, and if you are rusty in the fundamentals of electrical engineering concepts and principles, then this two (2) day course could serve as a <strong>&ldquo;warm-up&rdquo;</strong> on some of the electrical engineering principles, concepts and problem analyses techniques.</li>
</ol>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>
<p>Leadership and Professional Development</p>

			<div style="margin-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--40);" class="wp-block-post-date has-small-font-size"><time datetime="2026-04-03T00:52:19+00:00"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/electrical-engineering-principles-and-practices-for-non-electrical-engineers-mce-opd-c-eenee/">April 3, 2026</a></time></div>
		</div>
		
	</li><li class="wp-block-post post-80 imported_item type-imported_item status-publish hentry">
		
		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/national-electrical-code-nfpa-70-intro-review-and-update-mce-opd-c-necnfpa/" target="_self" >National Electrical Code NFPA 70 Intro, Review and Update &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-NECNFPA</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>National Electrical Code NFPA 70 Intro, Review and Update<br />
MCE-OPD-C-NECNFPA</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>This course covers key articles of the NFPA 70, aka, The National Electrical Code, and an update of 2023 changes. This course is designed so that even non-electrical engineers and non-electricians can learn the basic tenets of the NEC. Upon attending this course, participants will be able to identify codes pertaining to various electrical equipment installations. Participants will learn the methodology associated with analyzing and interpreting key articles in the National Electrical Code. Some key calculations related to the application of the code will be illustrated, followed by class exercises for knowledge reinforcement purposes. The main focus of this course is low voltage (0 to 1000V). The major updates in the 2023 revision of the code will be covered. In order to enhance the participants&rsquo; understanding of the line current differences between three-phase AC, &ldquo;Y&rdquo; and &ldquo;&#8710; &#8211; Delta&rdquo; configurations &#8211; in the selection and application of protective devices &#8211; methods for calculating three-phase AC currents in &ldquo;Y&rdquo; and &ldquo;&#8710; &#8211; Delta&rdquo; loads will be covered. This course is designed for electrical engineers, non-electrical engineers with some electrical background, licensed electrical professional engineers, maintenance engineers, engineering managers, facilities managers and other professionals who are not familiar or current on National Electrical Code. This 8-hour review of the NEC is an abridged version of the typical one-week comprehensive course. Board acceptance guarantee. The audience is engaged through Q&amp;A, classwork, and ad hoc discussions pertaining to the topic.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Who Should Attend</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Licensed Professional Engineers</strong>, who need to meet the annual or biennial license renewal PDH (Professional Development Hour) or CEU (Continuing Education Units) requirements</li>
<li><strong>Engineers and architects</strong> who do not possess a current working knowledge of the NEC</li>
<li><strong>Facility managers, engineering managers, program/project managers and other professionals</strong> who feel a lack of adequate familiarity with the NEC to hold meaningful discussions and to make informed decisions when interacting with their electrical subordinates or colleagues</li>
<li><strong>Procurement/purchasing professionals</strong> who are responsible for acquisition of electrical installation services</li>
<li>Candidates aspiring to take the <strong>FE or PE exams</strong></li>
<li><strong>Construction managers</strong></li>
<li><strong>Maintenance engineers and maintenance managers</strong></li>
<li><strong>Other professionals</strong> whose annual PLP, Performance and Learning Program, includes engineering/technical courses/seminars/workshops</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>8 PDHs/0.8&nbsp;CEUs&nbsp;(7.5 PDHs for NYS Lic.)</li>
<li>Reference notebook with activities</li>
<li>Networking luncheon and breaks</li>
<li>Certificate&nbsp;of completion from NC&nbsp;State University</li>
</ul>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Why you shouldn&rsquo;t miss this course</strong> &ndash; how this course can benefit you, your organizations, and what is unique about this course:</p>
<ol>
<li>Have you ever felt somewhat inadequate and ill-equipped in your <strong>technical, electrical code-related discussions with electrical engineers and electricians</strong>? If so, then this course is a must.</li>
<li>Do you <strong>feel that your knowledge and understanding of the electrical code</strong> is inadequate or insufficient?&nbsp;&nbsp;Then you must not miss this course.</li>
<li>If you are familiar with the NEC but would like to <strong>refresh yourself</strong> on the code and also <strong>learn about the&nbsp;updates</strong>, then&nbsp;this course presents an excellent opportunity.</li>
<li>How often do you get a chance to attend a workshop, course, or a seminar that is presented by the author of book on related subject matter &#8211; live? In this seminar, you will have the opportunity to interact and learn from <strong>Bobby Rauf, the author of the text, titled, &ldquo;Electrical Engineering for Non-Electrical Engineers.&rdquo;&nbsp;</strong></li>
<li>As an electrical engineer, <strong>do you find various articles of the NEC elusive</strong> and hard to comprehend? Then, this seminar will present an excellent opportunity to remedy that.&nbsp; &nbsp;</li>
<li>Some workshops and seminars end up being monotonous monologues from the presenter to the audience. Not this one. <strong>In this seminar, you will get an opportunity to exercise the skills and concepts through classwork and engage the instructor in discussions.</strong></li>
<li>Last, but not least &ndash; If you are <strong><em>not</em></strong> a licensed Professional Engineer, but aspire to be one, and if you are rusty on the comprehension and application of the National Electrical Code &ndash; which is a key component of the NCEES&reg; Electrical Professional Engineering Examination &#8211; then this two (2) day course could supplement your preparation for the PE examination.&nbsp;</li>
</ol>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>
<p>Leadership and Professional Development</p>
</div>
			<div style="margin-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--40);" class="wp-block-post-date has-small-font-size"><time datetime="2026-04-03T00:52:19+00:00"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/national-electrical-code-nfpa-70-intro-review-and-update-mce-opd-c-necnfpa/">April 3, 2026</a></time></div>
		</div>
		
	</li><li class="wp-block-post post-81 imported_item type-imported_item status-publish hentry">
		
		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/insect-rearing-system-fundamentals-mce-opd-c-olfirsf/" target="_self" >Insect Rearing System Fundamentals &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-OLFIRSF</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Insect Rearing System Fundamentals<br />
MCE-OPD-C-OLFIRSF</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>Click on the picture to play the video.<br />
<a href="http://youtube.com/watch?v=QGX9n6uhOgw" target="_blank"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" width="1440" height="813" alt="Insect Rearing System Fundamentals -- online course" src="http://localhost:8080/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/insect-rearing-video-scrnshot-spring-26.png" style="height:363px; width:643px" class="wp-image-82" srcset="https://host.docker.internal/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/insect-rearing-video-scrnshot-spring-26.png 1440w, https://host.docker.internal/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/insect-rearing-video-scrnshot-spring-26-300x169.png 300w, https://host.docker.internal/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/insect-rearing-video-scrnshot-spring-26-1024x578.png 1024w, https://host.docker.internal/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/insect-rearing-video-scrnshot-spring-26-768x434.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1440px) 100vw, 1440px" /></a></p>
<p>This course is an examination of the fundamental aspects of insect rearing where you will study what makes insect diets succeed, and how environmental factors (such as temperature, humidity, air exchange, light conditions, and microbes) are involved in the quality and stability of insect rearing procedures. This course will also include the genetics and epigenetics of insect rearing and how the various components interact. A major emphasis in this course is how you may identify and treat stress inflicted on our reared insects and how eliminating stress helps define a high-quality product.</p>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>2.4&nbsp;CEUs / 24&nbsp;PDHs</li>
<li>A certificate of completion from NC State University</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Recommended Supplementary Reading</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Cohen, A. C. 2015.&nbsp;<em>Insect Diets: Science and Technology</em>. 2nd Edition. CRC Press. Boca Raton, FL.</li>
<li>Cohen, A. C. 2020. <em>Design, Operations, and Control of Insect Rearing Systems</em>. CRC Press. Boca Raton, FL</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>*</strong>By registering for this course, you will be subscribed to our newsletter and other communications to receive updates and resources about future courses. You can unsubscribe at any time.&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>
<p>Leadership and Professional Development</p>

			<div style="margin-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--40);" class="wp-block-post-date has-small-font-size"><time datetime="2026-04-03T00:52:19+00:00"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/insect-rearing-system-fundamentals-mce-opd-c-olfirsf/">April 3, 2026</a></time></div>
		</div>
		
	</li><li class="wp-block-post post-37 imported_item type-imported_item status-publish hentry">
		
		<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">
			
			<h2 class="wp-block-post-title has-x-large-font-size"><a href="https://host.docker.internal/imported-item/facilities-engineering-management-3-mce-opd-c-zffem3/" target="_self" >Facilities Engineering Management 3 &#8211; MCE-OPD-C-ZFFEM3</a></h2>
			<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-medium-font-size has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained"><p>Facilities Engineering Management 3<br />
MCE-OPD-C-ZFFEM3</p>
<p>Description</p>
<p>Facilities Engineering Management (FEM) 3&nbsp;is part of the <a href="https://reporter.ncsu.edu/link/ProgramSignUp?ProgramID=MCE-OPD-C-FEMDIPLOMA" target="_blank">Facilities Engineering Management Diploma</a> program, designed&nbsp;to provide facility maintenance management professionals&nbsp;with the knowledge you need to help your facility reach its goals. In FEM 3,&nbsp;you will concentrate on maintenance management techniques,&nbsp;improving maintenance functions,&nbsp;engineering issues in facilities management,&nbsp;building automation systems,&nbsp;trends in renewable energy generation,&nbsp;HVAC maintenance,&nbsp;and building commissioning.</p>
<p>Tailor your learning experience to your needs and choose from the following topics:</p>
<ul>
<li>Working with contractors: design and build contracts</li>
<li>OSHA 10-hour construction certification</li>
<li>Fundamentals of commercial and industrial roofing</li>
<li>Guide to building automation</li>
<li>Energy-efficient motors and VFDs</li>
<li>HVAC maintenance techniques for facilities managers</li>
<li>Trends in renewable generation</li>
<li>The existing building commissioning process</li>
</ul>
<p>
<a href="https://reporter.ncsu.edu/link/ProgramSignUp?ProgramID=MCE-OPD-C-FEMDIPLOMA"><strong>About the FEM Diploma Program</strong></a><br />
Three&nbsp;one-week courses&ndash;totaling&nbsp;96 contact hours&#8211;will provide you with critical, money-saving&nbsp;skills in the areas of maintenance, electrical, mechanical, environmental, health and safety, construction, energy conservation, and management material. The weekly sessions, or equivalent hours, do not have to be taken in sequence. Upon the completion of the requirements, you will be expected to make a final presentation (15 minutes) on your special experiences in the field of facilities management. You will then be awarded a non-degree diploma from NC State&#8217;s Office of Professional Development.</p>
<p>Course Notes</p>
<p><strong>Who Should Attend</strong><br />
The FEM Diploma Program is intended for managers of maintenance, maintenance supervisors, maintenance technicians with operations responsibilities, plant and facility engineers, maintenance planners and anyone who makes maintenance decisions regarding operations, repair or replacement.</p>
<p><strong>Attend and You Will Receive</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A comprehensive reference notebook you can use every day on the job</li>
<li>A tote bag to carry your class materials</li>
<li>4 networking luncheons and daily refreshment breaks (in-person classes only)</li>
<li>A Certificate of Completion</li>
<li>3.2 CEUs/32 PDHs</li>
<li>You will&nbsp;receive an OSHA 10-Hour Construction Certification card</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Approved Course Provider for the Federal Buildings Personnel Training Act</strong></p>
<p><strong>Download or view:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://go.ncsu.edu/fem-brochure" target="_blank"><strong>Brochure</strong></a></li>
<li><a href="https://projects.coned.ncsu.edu/opd/floorplan/FEM%20Registration%20Form.pdf"><strong>Registration form</strong></a></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Diploma Programs That May Interest You:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://learn.mckimmoncenter.ncsu.edu/search/publicCourseSearchDetails.do?method=load&amp;courseId=11862" target="_blank">Facilities Engineering Management&nbsp;</a><a href="https://reporter.ncsu.edu/link/ProgramSignUp?ProgramID=MCE-OPD-C-FEMDIPLOMA">Diploma Program</a></li>
<li><a href="https://reporter.ncsu.edu/link/ProgramSignUp?ProgramID=MCE-OPD-C-EMDIPLOMA" target="_blank">Energy Management Diploma Program</a></li>
<li><a href="https://reporter.ncsu.edu/link/ProgramSignUp?ProgramID=MCE-OPD-MRM" target="_blank">Maintenance and Reliability Management Diploma</a></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note: By registering for this course, you will be subscribed to our newsletter and other communications to receive updates and resources about future courses. You can unsubscribe at any time.</strong></p>
<p>Subject Areas</p>
<p>Training Category</p>

  4. Risk=Informational, Confidence=Low (3)

    1. https://host.docker.internal (3)

      1. Charset Mismatch (1)
        1. GET https://host.docker.internal/wp-json/oembed/1.0/embed?format=xml&url=https%3A%2F%2Fhost.docker.internal%2Fkurilian%2F
          Alert tags
          • CWE-436
          • POLICY_QA_STD =
          • POLICY_PENTEST =
          • SYSTEMIC
          Alert description

          This check identifies responses where the HTTP Content-Type header declares a charset different from the charset defined by the body of the HTML or XML. When there's a charset mismatch between the HTTP header and content body Web browsers can be forced into an undesirable content-sniffing mode to determine the content's correct character set.

          An attacker could manipulate content on the page to be interpreted in an encoding of their choice. For example, if an attacker can control content at the beginning of the page, they could inject script using UTF-7 encoded text and manipulate some browsers into interpreting that text.
          Other info

          There was a charset mismatch between the HTTP Header and the XML encoding declaration: [UTF-8] and [null] do not match.

      2. Cookie Poisoning (1)
        1. GET https://host.docker.internal/wp-login.php?loggedout=true&wp_lang=en_US
          Alert tags
          • CWE-565
          • OWASP_2021_A03
          • POLICY_QA_STD =
          • POLICY_PENTEST =
          • SYSTEMIC
          • OWASP_2017_A01
          • POLICY_DEV_STD =
          Alert description

          This check looks at user-supplied input in query string parameters and POST data to identify where cookie parameters might be controlled. This is called a cookie poisoning attack, and becomes exploitable when an attacker can manipulate the cookie in various ways. In some cases this will not be exploitable, however, allowing URL parameters to set cookie values is generally considered a bug.
          Other info

          An attacker may be able to poison cookie values through URL parameters. Try injecting a semicolon to see if you can add cookie values (e.g. name=controlledValue;name=anotherValue;).

          This was identified at:

          https://host.docker.internal/wp-login.php?loggedout=true&wp_lang=en_US

          wp_lang=en_US; path=/; secure; HttpOnly

          wp_lang=en_US

<div class="wp-block-group alignfull has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained" style="padding-top:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60);padding-bottom:var(--wp--preset--spacing--60)">

<h1 class="wp-block-post-title">Privacy Policy</h1>

<div class="entry-content alignfull wp-block-post-content has-global-padding is-layout-constrained wp-block-post-content-is-layout-constrained">
<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Who we are</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>Our website address is: http://localhost:8080.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Comments</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>When visitors leave comments on the site we collect the data shown in the comments form, and also the visitor&#8217;s IP address and browser user agent string to help spam detection.</p>


<p>An anonymized string created from your email address (also called a hash) may be provided to the Gravatar service to see if you are using it. The Gravatar service privacy policy is available here: https://automattic.com/privacy/. After approval of your comment, your profile picture is visible to the public in the context of your comment.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Media</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>If you upload images to the website, you should avoid uploading images with embedded location data (EXIF GPS) included. Visitors to the website can download and extract any location data from images on the website.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Cookies</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>If you leave a comment on our site you may opt-in to saving your name, email address and website in cookies. These are for your convenience so that you do not have to fill in your details again when you leave another comment. These cookies will last for one year.</p>


<p>If you visit our login page, we will set a temporary cookie to determine if your browser accepts cookies. This cookie contains no personal data and is discarded when you close your browser.</p>


<p>When you log in, we will also set up several cookies to save your login information and your screen display choices. Login cookies last for two days, and screen options cookies last for a year. If you select &quot;Remember Me&quot;, your login will persist for two weeks. If you log out of your account, the login cookies will be removed.</p>


<p>If you edit or publish an article, an additional cookie will be saved in your browser. This cookie includes no personal data and simply indicates the post ID of the article you just edited. It expires after 1 day.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Embedded content from other websites</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>Articles on this site may include embedded content (e.g. videos, images, articles, etc.). Embedded content from other websites behaves in the exact same way as if the visitor has visited the other website.</p>


<p>These websites may collect data about you, use cookies, embed additional third-party tracking, and monitor your interaction with that embedded content, including tracking your interaction with the embedded content if you have an account and are logged in to that website.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Who we share your data with</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>If you request a password reset, your IP address will be included in the reset email.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">How long we retain your data</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>If you leave a comment, the comment and its metadata are retained indefinitely. This is so we can recognize and approve any follow-up comments automatically instead of holding them in a moderation queue.</p>


<p>For users that register on our website (if any), we also store the personal information they provide in their user profile. All users can see, edit, or delete their personal information at any time (except they cannot change their username). Website administrators can also see and edit that information.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">What rights you have over your data</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>If you have an account on this site, or have left comments, you can request to receive an exported file of the personal data we hold about you, including any data you have provided to us. You can also request that we erase any personal data we hold about you. This does not include any data we are obliged to keep for administrative, legal, or security purposes.</p>


<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Where your data is sent</h2>


<p><strong class="privacy-policy-tutorial">Suggested text: </strong>Visitor comments may be checked through an automated spam detection service.</p>

</div>

<script id="wp-block-template-skip-link-js-after">
	( function() {
		var skipLinkTarget = document.querySelector( 'main' ),
			sibling,
			skipLinkTargetID,
			skipLink;

		// Early exit if a skip-link target can't be located.
		if ( ! skipLinkTarget ) {
			return;
		}

		/*
		 * Get the site wrapper.
		 * The skip-link will be injected in the beginning of it.
		 */
		sibling = document.querySelector( '.wp-site-blocks' );

		// Early exit if the root element was not found.
		if ( ! sibling ) {
			return;
		}

		// Get the skip-link target's ID, and generate one if it doesn't exist.
		skipLinkTargetID = skipLinkTarget.id;
		if ( ! skipLinkTargetID ) {
			skipLinkTargetID = 'wp--skip-link--target';
			skipLinkTarget.id = skipLinkTargetID;
		}

		// Create the skip link.
		skipLink = document.createElement( 'a' );
		skipLink.classList.add( 'skip-link', 'screen-reader-text' );
		skipLink.id = 'wp-skip-link';
		skipLink.href = '#' + skipLinkTargetID;
		skipLink.innerText = 'Skip to content';

		// Inject the skip link.
		sibling.parentElement.insertBefore( skipLink, sibling );
	}() );
	
//# sourceURL=wp-block-template-skip-link-js-after
</script>

Appendix

Alert Types

This section contains additional information on the types of alerts in the report.

  1. Path Traversal

    Source raised by an active scanner (plugin ID: 6)
    CWE ID 22
    WASC ID 33
    Reference
    1. https://owasp.org/www-community/attacks/Path_Traversal
    2. https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/22.html

  2. Big Redirect Detected (Potential Sensitive Information Leak)

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Big Redirect Detected (Potential Sensitive Information Leak))
    CWE ID 201
    WASC ID 13

  3. Private IP Disclosure

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Private IP Disclosure)
    CWE ID 497
    WASC ID 13
    Reference
    1. https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc1918

  4. Secure Pages Include Mixed Content

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Secure Pages Include Mixed Content)
    CWE ID 311
    WASC ID 4
    Reference
    1. https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Transport_Layer_Protection_Cheat_Sheet.html

  5. Charset Mismatch

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Charset Mismatch)
    CWE ID 436
    WASC ID 15
    Reference
    1. https://code.google.com/archive/p/browsersec/wikis/Part2.wiki#Character_set_handling_and_detection

  6. Cookie Poisoning

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Cookie Poisoning)
    CWE ID 565
    WASC ID 20
    Reference
    1. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTP_cookie
    2. https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/565.html

  7. Information Disclosure - Suspicious Comments

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Information Disclosure - Suspicious Comments)
    CWE ID 615
    WASC ID 13

  8. Session Management Response Identified

    Source raised by a passive scanner (Session Management Response Identified)
    Reference
    1. https://www.zaproxy.org/docs/desktop/addons/authentication-helper/session-mgmt-id/

  9. User Controllable HTML Element Attribute (Potential XSS)

    Source raised by a passive scanner (User Controllable HTML Element Attribute (Potential XSS))
    CWE ID 20
    WASC ID 20
    Reference
    1. https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Input_Validation_Cheat_Sheet.html
